                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">نَارٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form> a word of which the meaning is well known; (M, K;) [<hi rend="ital">Fire;</hi> not well explained as signifying] the <hi rend="ital">flaming,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">blazing,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">لَهِيب</foreign>,) <hi rend="ital">that is apparent to the sense:</hi> (TA:) its <foreign lang="ar">ا</foreign> is originally <foreign lang="ar">نُوَيْرَةٌ</foreign>: (S, TA:) it is fem.: (S, M, Msb:) and sometimes masc.: (AHn, M, K:) and the dim. is <foreign lang="ar">أَنْوَارٌ</foreign>, with <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> because it is the original medial radical, (S,) and with <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> because <foreign lang="ar">نار</foreign> is fem.: (Msb:) pl. [of pauc.] <foreign lang="ar">أَنْوُرٌ</foreign>, (S, M, L,) in the K <foreign lang="ar">أَنْوَارٌ</foreign>, [which is a mistake, though this is also said to be a pl. of <foreign lang="ar">نار</foreign>,] (TA,) and [of mult.] <foreign lang="ar">نِيرَانٌ</foreign> [which is the most common form] (S, M, K) and <foreign lang="ar">نُورٌ</foreign> (AAF, S, M, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">نِيَرَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">نِيَارٌ</foreign>, (M, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَنْيَارٌ</foreign> also occurs, in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">نَارُ الأَنْيَارِ</foreign>, in a trad. respecting the prison of hell; this phrase, if correctly related, perhaps meaning <foreign lang="ar">نَارُ النِّيِرَانِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">انيار</foreign> being originally <foreign lang="ar">أَنْوَار</foreign>. (IAth.) <foreign lang="ar">النَّارُ</foreign> is also applied to <hi rend="ital">The fire of hell.</hi> (TA:) The Arabs say, in cursing their enemies, <foreign lang="ar">أَبْعَدَ ٱللّٰهُ دَارَهُمْ وَأَوْقَدَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">نَارًا أَثَرَهُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">May God make their abode distant, and kindle a fire after them!</hi>] And it was a custom of Arab women, as related by IAar, on the authority of El-'Okeyleeyeh, when they feared evil from a man, and he removed from them, to kindle a fire behind him, with the view of causing his evil to depart with him. (T.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">نَارُ ٱلْمُهَوِّلِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">A fire which the Arabs used to kindle, in the time of ignorance, on the occasion of entering into a confederacy: they threw into it some salt, which crackled</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">يُفَقِّعُ</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">when the fire burned it: with this they frightened</hi> [<hi rend="ital">one another</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in confirmation of the swearing.</hi> (T.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">نَارُ الحُبَاحِبِ</foreign> has been explained in art. <foreign lang="ar">حب</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">نَارٌ</foreign> also signifies simply <hi rend="ital">Heat.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  Also, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [The <hi rend="ital">fire,</hi> meaning] the <hi rend="ital">evil, and excitement,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">rage,</hi> or war; as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40724-1" target="نَائِرَةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">أَوْقَدَ نَارَ الحَرْبِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He kindled the fire of war</hi>]. (A.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  Also, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Opinion; counsel; advice.</hi> (IAar, T, K.) So in the trad., <foreign lang="ar">لَا تَسْتَضِيؤُوا بِنَارِ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">المُشْرِكِينَ</foreign>, (T,) or <foreign lang="ar">بنار أَهْلِ الشِّرْكِ</foreign>, (K,) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">Seek ye not to enlighten yourselves by the counsel of the polytheists;</hi> i. e.,] <hi rend="ital">seek ye not counsel of the polytheists.</hi> (IAar, T, A. *)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  Also, <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Any brand,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mark, made with a hot iron, upon a camel;</hi> (As, T, S, M, A, K;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40724-2" target="نُورَةٌ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n40728"/></foreign> (M, K) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40724-3" target="نُورٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n40726"/></foreign>: (TA:) pl. as above: (M:) or the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">نِيَارٌ</foreign>, and the pl. of the <foreign lang="ar">نار</foreign> that burns is <foreign lang="ar">نِيرَانٌ</foreign>. (IAar, Th, T.) The Arabs say, <foreign lang="ar">مَا نَارُ هٰذِهِ النَّاقَةِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">What is the brand,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mark, of this she-camel, with which she is burned?</hi> (T, S, A. *) And they say, in a proverb, <foreign lang="ar">بِجَارُهَا نَارُهَا</foreign> (T, S) <hi rend="ital">Their origin is indicated by their mark with which they are burned.</hi> (T.) The Rájiz says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">حَتَّى سَقَوْا آبَالَهُمْ بِالنَّارِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَالنَّارُ قَدْ تَشْفِى مِنَ الأُوَارِ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Until,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">so that, they watered their camels because of the brand that they bore: for the fire,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the brand, sometimes cures of the heat of thirst</hi>]: (T, S: *) he means, that, when they saw their marks with which they were burned, they left the water to them.                   <hi rend="ital">Light;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">ضِيَآءٌ</foreign>, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">ضَوْءٌ</foreign>; (M, A, Msb, K;) <hi rend="ital">whatever it be;</hi> (M, A, K;) <hi rend="ital">contr. of</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ظُلْمَةٌ</foreign>: (Msb:) or the <hi rend="ital">rays thereof:</hi> (M, A, K:) accord to Z, <foreign lang="ar">ضِيَآءٌ</foreign> [with which <foreign lang="ar">ضَوْءٌ</foreign> is syn.] is more intense than <foreign lang="ar">نُورٌ</foreign>: in the Kur, x. 5, the sun is termed <foreign lang="ar">ضياء</foreign>, and the moon <foreign lang="ar">نور</foreign>: and it is said that <foreign lang="ar">ضياء</foreign> is essential, but <foreign lang="ar">نور</foreign> is <hi rend="ital">accidental</hi> [<hi rend="ital">light</hi>]: (TA:) it is of two kinds, the light of the present world and that of the world to come; and the former is either perceived sensibly, by the eye, and this is what diffuses itself from luminous bodies, as the sun and moon and stars, and is mentioned in the Kur, x. 5, referred to above; or perceived by the eye of the intellect, and this is what diffuses itself of the divine lights, as the light of reason and the light of the Kur-án; of which divine light mention is made in the Kur, v., former part of verse 18, and xxiv., latter part of verse 35; and both of these in common are spoken of in the Kur, vi. 1 and xxxix. 69: that of the world to come is mentioned in the Kur in lvii. 12 [and lxvi. 8]: (B:) the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أَنْوَارٌ</foreign> (S, M, Msb, K) and <foreign lang="ar">نِيرَانٌ</foreign>; (M, K;) the latter mentioned by Th: (M:) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n40726-1" target="نَوْرَانيَّةٌ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">نُورٌ</foreign>. (TA.) As <foreign lang="ar">نور</foreign> is a convenience of the pious in the present world and the world to come, it is said in the Kur, [lvii. 13,] <foreign lang="ar">اُنْظُرُونَا نَقْتَبِسْ مِنْ نُورِكُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Wait ye for us that we may take of your light</hi>]. (B.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">ظُلَمْةٌ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  It is also applied to <hi rend="ital">Mohammad:</hi> (T, M, K:) it is said by Aboo-Is-hak to be so applied in the Kur, v. 18. (T.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  And That <hi rend="ital">which manifests things,</hi> (K, TA,) <hi rend="ital">and shows to the eyes their true</hi> or <hi rend="ital">real state:</hi> and therefore <foreign lang="ar">النُّور</foreign> is applied in the Kur, vii. 156, to <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">that</hi> [<hi rend="ital">revelation</hi>] <hi rend="ital">which the Prophet brought.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">النُّورُ</foreign> is also one of the names of God; meaning, accord. to IAth, <hi rend="ital">He by whose light the obscure in perception sees, and by whose guidance the erring is directed aright:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the Manifest, by whom is every manifestation.</hi> And <foreign lang="ar">أَللّٰهُ نُورُ السَّمٰوَاتِ وَٱلْأَرْضِ</foreign> [in the Kur, xxiv. 35,] means <hi rend="ital">God is the enlightener of the heavens and of the earth:</hi> like as <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ غِيَاثُنَا</foreign> means <foreign lang="ar">مُغِيثُنَا</foreign>: (TA:) or, as some say, <hi rend="ital">the right director of the inhabitants of the heavens and of the inhabitants of the earth.</hi> (T.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">نَارٌ</foreign>, last signification. <pb n="2866"/>

K.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A sign,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">mark, set up to show the way:</hi> (As, T, S, M, K:) and <hi rend="ital">a thing that is put as a limit</hi> or <hi rend="ital">boundary between two things;</hi> (M, K;) or <hi rend="ital">between two lands,</hi> (As, T,) <hi rend="ital">made of mud</hi> or <hi rend="ital">clay</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of earth:</hi> (As, TA:) pl. <foreign lang="ar">مَنَاثِرُ</foreign> [respecting which see <foreign lang="ar">مَنَارَةٌ</foreign>]. (A.) It is [also used as a coll. gen. n.; as, for instance, where it is] said, in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">لَعَنَ ٱللّٰهُ مَنْ غَيَّرَ مَنَارَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الأَرْضِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">May God curse him who alters the marks of the limit between two lands:</hi> (T, TA:) or it may mean <foreign lang="ar">مَنَارَ الحَرَمِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">the boundary-marks of the Haram</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">sacred territory</hi> of Mekkeh], which [it is said] were set up by Abraham. (T, TA. *) And it is said in another trad, <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّ لِلْإِسْلَامِ صُوًى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَمَنَارًا</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Verily there are to El-Islám signs and ordinances whereby it is known.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  See also <foreign lang="ar">صَوْمَعَةٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  The <hi rend="ital">middle,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">main part and middle,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">part along which one travels,</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">مَحَجَّة</foreign>,) of a road. (M, K.)    </entryFree>30:T946,<entryFree id="n40738" key="مَنَارَةٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">مَنَارَةٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, originally <foreign lang="ar">مَنْوَرَةٌ</foreign>; (A, K;) see <foreign lang="ar">مَنَارٌ</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <hi rend="ital">A stand for a lamp; a thing upon which a lamp is put:</hi> (T, S, M, A, K;) of the measure <foreign lang="ar">مَفْعَلَةٌ</foreign>. with fet-h (S, Msb) to the <foreign lang="ar">م</foreign>; (S:) but by rule it should be with kesr, because it is an instrument (Msb.) Aboo-Dhu-eyb uses it, for the sake of metre, in the place of <foreign lang="ar">مِصْبَاح</foreign>, in likening a bright spear-head, without rust, to a lamp. (M.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  Also, <hi rend="ital">A candle having a</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">سِرَاج</foreign> [or <hi rend="ital">lighted wick</hi>]. (T.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [<hi rend="ital">A pharos,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">lighthouse.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  The <hi rend="ital">mená reh</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">turret of a mosque,</hi> whence the English term “ minaret, ” so written in imitation of the Turkish pronunciation,] <hi rend="ital">upon which the time of prayer is proclaimed;</hi> (S, Msb:) syn. <foreign lang="ar">مِئْذَنَةٌ</foreign>, (K, TA,) vulgarly <foreign lang="ar">مَأَذَنَةٌ</foreign> [which is the form given in the CK]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  [<hi rend="ital">Any pillar-like structure.</hi> (See <foreign lang="ar">زُرْنُوقٌ</foreign>.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  The <hi rend="ital">perch</hi> of a hawk, or falcon. (See <foreign lang="ar">مَرْبَأٌ</foreign>.)]          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  The pl. is <foreign lang="ar">مَنَاوِرُ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَنَائِرُ</foreign>: he who uses the latter likens the radical letter to the augmentative; (S, Msb, K;) like as they say <foreign lang="ar">مَصَائِبُ</foreign>, which is originally <foreign lang="ar">مَصَاوِبُ</foreign> (S, Msb.)
